Around the World in 30 Decks
============================



 Posted in [Reconstructed](/en/articles/columns/reconstructed-archive)
 on May 26, 2015 






![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/styles/auth_small/public/images/person/authorPic_GavinVerhey.jpg)
By Gavin Verhey




 When Gavin Verhey was eleven, he dreamt of a job making Magic cards—and now as a Magic designer, he's living his dream! Gavin has been writing about Magic since 2005. 






I live in one corner of one country, on one continent, on one planet. There, I live inside a city, on a small street, in a home. Globally, I am but a speck. A tiny little blip, making runs to and from my house and work, and back again.



But yet, if you were to draw lines on the globe from me to the connections around the world I make every day and the global discussions I have, you could see this spider-web trail from space. And then, if you were to go a step further, and put little red dots on every person playing the same game I was, thinking about the same cards that I am, you would light up the earth.



*Magic* is the link that connects us all.



It's easy to forget how much of a shared language it is. How much we take for granted that this game—this game that is really so much more than just a game—weaves us all together like the fibers in an artisanal basket. And that around the world, hundreds upon thousands upon *millions* of players are thinking about the same cards you are, the same formats you are, the same deck building decisions you are, the same "Should I [Roast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Roast) this Courser or wait for a [Siege Rhino](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Siege+Rhino)?" moments that you are.



It's amazing to be part of a community that is so well represented around the world on every single continent. Yet, despite our separation, and despite our differences, we all have so much in common thanks to this marvelous game.



And every week, ReConstructed serves as a sort of hub. A decklist ocean that rivers from around the world pour their *Magic*al energies into.



In the deck building challenge two weeks ago, I told readers they could submit whatever they wanted as long as they included which country they were from. Today, I want to take a decklist tour of the world and show just how wide *Magic* is…and how you can find both differences and similarities everywhere you look.



Today is a celebration of my readers and their decklists from around the world. It's time to let all of your decklists and innovations really shine!



Ready? Well, hop on board this ride and get ready to head out. We've got a journey around the world in front of us!





---

United States of America
========================



When a lot of people think of *Magic*, they think of the United States. This melting pot of a country is home to plenty of *Magic* history—including many of the early pro players, and, of course, where I'm writing this now, Wizards of the Coast out in Renton, Washington.



This means you have players from all over the country playing all kinds of different formats. Everything from casual to competitive; brewers and tuners alike.



Of course, you have people who like to play with the red, white, and blue:

99 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Narset%2C+Enlightened+Master)

















Commander is very popular here as the casual format of choice. And all flag-coincidences aside, Narset in particular has been all over Commander recently, a powerful tool to flip up a ton of extra damage. (Plus, Narset is awesome.)





---

Of course, some people prefer no color at all:

99 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Kozilek%2C+Butcher+of+Truth)

















It looks like with *Battle for Zendikar* on the horizon, Andrew is getting excited to revisit the last time we were on Zendikar with *Rise of the Eldrazi*. An active participant in social media like Twitter and Tumblr, Andrew is an avid Commander fan and I see builds he talks about pop up quite often.





---

Of course, it's not just all Commander! There's always good 'ol fashioned casual *Magic*.



Mike out in South Carolina just likes to shuffle up his casual 60-card decks with his friends. As he put it to me in his email, it's something where he can maintain the same deck forever and just "pull some cards together and go have some fun."

![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Avenger+of+Zendikar)

















Longtime reader Travis Froggrat is the same way. He likes casual because, as he says, "it's the only place I can play my favorite deck." It's not quite strong enough for Legacy, but "it's caused at least one pilot to jump out of his chair, arms thrown up into the air, storming away from the table for a few seconds, in total disbelief at the deck's level of synergy."



And hey, that's always a win in my book.








#### Travis Froggatt's Grime & Sunlight

---

On the other hand, maybe you’re more of a Tribal Wars kind of person.



Though never really heavily supported with events, that doesn’t mean that if you enjoy a format you can’t try to get some friends into playing your idea too! (I should know—that’s partially how I landed my job at Wizards.)



Jonah Comstock’s playgroup? Well, their thing is Budget Star Tribal Wars. No, that’s not the name of the next epic space movie: it’s just a format where you have to build around a single color and a tribe in that color, on a budget, and then you play a five player game with a person playing each color. (For more on how Star Magic works, you can actually check out the rules as written by perennial DailyMTG member Kelly Digges in [the article he wrote about it](http://magic.wizards.com/en/articles/archive/serious-fun/star-power-2008-08-05).)








#### Jonah Comstock’s Devotion to Minotaurs

And at the absolute super-far end of the spectrum are niche formats.



I joked about "Mathy Leaders" on my Tumblr about a month ago, a format "where all of your cards have to have a collector number that is a prime number, and your starting deck size is any two digits of pi that are next to each other that you can recite to."



So, naturally, I was sent a deck for it. Anything is possible!

As you can tell, since *Magic* has such strong roots in the United States, there's all kind of casual *Magic* played around the country. People who have played for over 20 years have their own playgroups and friends that have built up around the game, living in their own corner of the world, slinging cards from *Alpha* and *Mirage* to play the kind of game they enjoy most.





---

Of course, that's far from all there is. There's plenty of tournament play too! Everything from hardened qualifier-circuit players, who will play only what they feel are the top decks, to deck brewers who are always looking to figure out the next big thing.



Like Addison, for example:

2
[Heliod, God of the Sun](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BHeliod,%5D+%5BGod%5D+%5Bof%5D+%5Bthe%5D+%5BSun%5D)

75 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Sylvan+Caryatid)

















[Skybind](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Skybind) with manifests? Oh yes! [Flicker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Flicker) them out, and they'll come back in face up. If you want to keep triggering your [Hornet Queen](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hornet+Queen)s, that's certainly an option—or if you just want to slide out your face-down [Banishing Light](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Banishing+Light) and have it come back face-up and trigger [Skybind](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Skybind) *yet again*, that's certainly a thing you can do!



Ah, I love decks like this.





---

And let's not leave Modern out either. One of my favorite formats shows up plenty in the US. So it's time to end this section the same way we began: with a red, white, and blue deck. And hey, his name is Gavin!

Prowess with "free" Phyrexian mana spells like [Gitaxian Probe](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gitaxian+Probe) and cheap cantrips? Sign me up! This deck looks like a blast.



Okay, so that was a good tour around the USA. And, being an English article, that's certainly where a lot of my readers come from—but far, far from all of them. Hold onto your Reconstructed-reading-vessel, because we're about to head to Japan! (Imagine a cool *wooshing* noise here for added effect.)





---

Japan
=====



One of my favorite countries in the world is Japan. It's home to delicious food, awesome people great public transport, my favorite Disney theme park, and, perhaps most of all, some very creative deck builders that like to send exciting, unique decks to my inbox.



Now, that's not to say that I don't receive plenty of more typical decklists from Japan too—but there are many that stand out as paragons of creativity.



For example, check out this deck which stops your opponent from searching their library and then drops down a [Boldwyr Heavyweights](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Boldwyr+Heavyweights).

Cast a [Suture Priest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Suture+Priest) or [Blood Seeker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Blood+Seeker), then go to town, using cards like [Mercy Killing](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mercy+Killing) and [Hunted Phantasm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hunted+Phantasm) to hook your opponent up with plenty of tokens.

Unlike the last deck, this one wants to follow the more traditional plan of giving yourself tokens. Make a bunch of tokens, then pump them up fast with battle cry. Pow!





---

Sometimes the elegance is in the simplicity. Sometimes, it's about merging two different archetypes together into something that's even crazier than either of the two parts. Would you ever merge Slivers and [Battle of Wits](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Battle+of+Wits)? Well, someone certainly did!

60 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Mulldrifter)

















If you've never seen this deck before, it makes unlimited mana with [Misthollow Griffin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Misthollow+Griffin) and [Food Chain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Food+Chain) and then…. Well, Emrakul is soon to follow.





---

It's far from just all older formats though. In fact, some of the Standard decks can be the most interesting! Restrictions breed creativity, after all.

60 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Chasm+Skulker)

















I love the +1/+1 counter themed decks—and this pairs that with a small splash for [Chasm Skulker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chasm+Skulker) which has huge synergies in the deck, along with being able to put it onto the battlefield with [Collected Company](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Collected+Company). That's a neat interaction!



Other times, you might see uses for some cards turned on their heads:

![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Liliana+Vess)

















[Whip of Erebos](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Whip+of+Erebos) in a deck like this isn't necessarily the most natural fit…but when you're playing enough creatures, it actually starts to do pretty solid work! Returning a Sidisi, anyone?





---

And at the end of the day, competitive *Magic* aside, there's still plenty of interest in more casual play as well.



Commander is certainly alive and well. Here's one list:








#### Hiroyuki Masuda's Scarecrogic

99 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Reaper+King)

















Interestingly, Hiroyuki notes that this one is made for duel Commander—or one-on-one Commander—which tends to be most popular in France, but he brought the concept into his local playgroup and now it's mostly what they play! Very cool.





---

49 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Yasova+Dragonclaw)

















Ah, what a wonderfully varied mix. There's plenty of innovation—and hopefully you can now take those ideas back to your corner of the world to use as well.





---

But we're far from done on our tour. Shall we hop over to the UK?



United Kingdom
==============



Every winter for the past three years, I've packed my bags and spent about two weeks in the UK. It keeps bringing me back time and time again—and I always try to play some *Magic* while I'm there. And with such an exuberant community that loves the game, I always have a blast!



I've received all kinds of decks from the UK, from casual to competitive and everything in between. This can be highlighted with just two Modern decks!



Some of the most fun decks are the ones of the casual-competitive spectrum, like this Bats deck for Modern which is a little more on the casual end:








#### Andrew Glenister's Spooky Bats


##### 




[![](https://web.archive.org/web/20160726232508im_/http://magic.wizards.com/sites/all/modules/features/wiz_bean_content_deck_list/icons/decklist_download.png)](/en/decklist/deck-list-aa8b562d31419d87d653421ec40cdf6e.txt?n=Andrew%20Glenister%27s%20Spooky%20Bats)

Play some Bats, flicker them out, and drain your opponent to death! Fun times.





---

While that's a bit more on the casual end, another deck to come in from the United Kingdom was on the other end of the Modern spectrum. There's also this [Gifts Ungiven](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gifts+Ungiven) deck from England, which Matthew has put plenty of competitive rigor behind:

3
[Liliana of the Veil](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BLiliana%5D+%5Bof%5D+%5Bthe%5D+%5BVeil%5D)

60 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Thoughtseize)

















Good 'ol Gifts decks. Plenty of one-ofs, value plays, and [Unburial Rites](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Unburial+Rites)-Elesh Norn to cause immense harm to creature decks. Notably, Liliana is something you don't see in a lot of Gifts decks—that's a nice piece as well.





---

Alright! That was quick tour through the UK—now it's time to hop around more of Europe!



The Netherlands
===============



The delicious, delicious Netherlands. The country actually has a restraining order against me because of all the delicious stroopwafels and pastries I ate the last time I was back there. (Okay, not really. Thanks goodness!)



The Dutch *Magic* scene is pretty solid, and has brought out several strong professional players in its history. The marvelous Jeff Van Egmond submits me decks all the time, and they're usually pretty well tuned and ready for tournament play:








#### Jeff van Egmond's Standard Jeskai Dragons

60 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Dragonlord+Ojutai)

















This looks like a great take on Jeskai, using efficient burn and utility spells alongside the strong Dragons in *Dragons of Tarkir* to make a tempo masterpiece. You could certainly slay some events with a deck like this!



But it's not just all qualifiers and Pro Tour trophies. There's a casual scene over there too! Check out this Thassa Tiny Leaders deck that's mostly lands!

Sweden
======



Moving on to Sweden, I received a submission from ReConstructed mainstay Qoarl. Every single week, with very few exceptions, Qoarl makes it a point to submit *at least* one deck—usually more—to ReConstructed. He's been featured a few times now…and he's shown off a range of casual to competitive; from pure fun to head-smashing.



Here's what he sent in this week:

![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Ixidor%2C+Reality+Sculptor)

















This fun archetype is all about manifesting huge creatures…and then turning them up for cheap! Ixidor captured my imagination back when I opened one up too, and it's great to see the same mechanic represented across so many years.





---

Spain
=====



Moving from the mountains of Switzerland to the sunny plains of Spain, there's plenty of *Magic* to be played!



Like Andrew Weisel, way back in the United States, Santi Chasca has also been thinking forward to the new *Battle for Zendikar* set by revisiting one of the first Zendikar's main mechanics: Allies!

[Hardened Scales](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BHardened%5D+%5BScales%5D)


4
[Harabaz Druid](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BHarabaz%5D+%5BDruid%5D)


4
[Kabira Evangel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BKabira%5D+%5BEvangel%5D)


1
[Talus Paladin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BTalus%5D+%5BPaladin%5D)


1
[Kazuul Warlord](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BKazuul%5D+%5BWarlord%5D)


1
[Turntimber Ranger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BTurntimber%5D+%5BRanger%5D)


2
[Gavony Township](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BGavony%5D+%5BTownship%5D)


60 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Hardened+Scales)

















Combining all of the +1/+1 counters of allies with both [Hardened Scales](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hardened+Scales) and [Inspiring Call](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inspiring+Call) is a nice synergy across time—something I love about Modern. A turn one [Hardened Scales](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hardened+Scales) makes your [Oran-Rief Survivalist](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Oran-Rief+Survivalist) a two mana 3/3…that only grows every time you cast an ally!



This deck looks like a blast to play. Every corner of the world truly has some great *Magic* innovations!





---

Speaking of places you might not expect as much *Magic*, it's time to work our path south—*way* south!



South Africa
============



Another place I hope to visit in the next year or two is South Africa, and I'm already looking forward to trying to find a game of *Magic* there!



David Edwards sent this Modern deck in, one that is based on an archetype that long ago sat at the top of Standard. Having a nonrotating format makes it a bit easier to keep something like this together even if you don't get to play as often. Take a look:

David notes that he would play 4 [Kokusho, the Evening Star](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kokusho%2C+the+Evening+Star) and 2 [Predator Dragon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Predator+Dragon) if he could—he just doesn't have them yet!



Still, you can build up your storm count and then cast a [Dragonstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dragonstorm) to search up a Bogardan foursome that will melt away 20 points of your opponent's life total. Brutal!





---

Now we're going to hop across the water once more, heading this time to…



Australia
=========



Welcome to the land down under!



Tony Youssef has been submitting rogue decks of all shapes and sizes to ReConstructed for a long time, and it's always a pleasure to see what he has to send in. The deck featured here showcases an infinite combo, assembling a combo with [Myr Moonvessel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Myr+Moonvessel), [Blasting Station](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Blasting+Station), and [Enduring Renewal](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Enduring+Renewal):

4
[Tempered Steel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BTempered%5D+%5BSteel%5D)


60 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Memnite)

















If you're looking for a rogue new Modern combo deck to refine, this might be right up your alley! You can just [Cranial Plating](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cranial+Plating) and [Tempered Steel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tempered+Steel) your opponent out with some draws…and if you get to cast [Enduring Renewal](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Enduring+Renewal), you can set up your combo. I might also try out [Arcbound Ravager](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Arcbound+Ravager) too, since with [Enduring Renewal](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Enduring+Renewal) you can sacrifice the Moonvessel over and over again to gain unlimited +1/+1 counters.





---

Alright, it's time for one final trip! (And, fortunately, no plane flight required.)



Canada
======



Oh, Canada! Living in Washington state, I've been up to Vancouver for many a tournament as well as flown to events there before. Good times! And, of course, the *Magic* scene is vibrant.



You can play plenty of any format you want in Canada. Standard? Sure. Draft? Absolutely. Legacy? Oh yes:

60 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Mox+Diamond)

















Ah, the good 'ol Lands deck. While a little soft to combo decks, this kind of strategy really can crush midrange or beatdown decks. And, of course, you can always just draw a hand that brings out a turn-three Marit Lage token from [Dark Depths](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Depths). That should do the trick!





---

And on the other end of the paradigm, you can have casual. Check out another morph deck for casual play that pulls on both [Time Spiral](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Time+Spiral) morphs and brand new cards:

[Zoetic Cavern](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Zoetic+Cavern) is certainly a great card to have around, being a card that easily triggers [Secret Plans](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Secret+Plans) and [Trail of Mystery](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Trail+of+Mystery). And really again, this highlights how awesome it is that across such great spans of time, you can still find synergies.




And hey, we're in Canada. So if you go down a little further, that means…



There and Back Again
====================



We've made it back to the United States, where I am right now! Phew. What a trip!



The crazy part is: This is just a fragment of my inbox on any given week. While I hit up every different country I received an email from this week, it was still only a small selection of the decks I was sent. And, moreover, on different weeks I've received decks from other far-flung corners of the world. It goes to show that *Magic* really is everywhere. We're all brought together by this wonderful gaming thread. I can travel to practically any country in the world, and know that I can find people there to play *Magic* with.



And I absolutely wouldn't have it any other way.





---

Speaking of worldwide community, now it's time to turn this over to you! There have been a ton of decks featured in this column today, in a smorgasbord of formats. To keep with the community theme, now it's on you to tweak one of your favorites and send it back my way to feature!



Here's the deck building mission for this week:



**Format:** Any, with the restrictions below



**Restrictions:** Your deck must be based on or inspired one of the decks in today's column. Please note which deck inspired it in your email.



**Deadline:** Monday, June 1, at 6 p.m. Pacific Time.



Submit all decklists by emailing me at [reconstructeddecks@gmail.com](mailto:reconstructeddecks@gmail.com).



Decklists should be submitted with YOURNAME's DECKNAME at the top. Underneath should be one card per line, with just a leading number. For example:




> 
> 12 Mountain
> 
> 
> 4 [Satyr Firedancer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Satyr+Firedancer)
> 
> 
> 3 [Ash Zealot](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ash+Zealot)
> 
> 
> 4 [Lightning Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lightning+Bolt)
> 
> 
> 



…and so on. Please don't use anything but a space to separate the card numbers and names—don't write "4x [Lightning Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lightning+Bolt)," for example. Well-formatted decklists have a much better chance of being read and making it into the column. Poorly formatted decklists are more likely to be ignored. (If I can't read your decklist, I certainly can't talk about it!)



I've shown you all of these decks—now which is your favorite? Which do you want me to talk about? That's in your hands! Look over them again and see which you want to work with the most!



In the meantime, if you have any feedback or questions on this article at all, I'd love to hear your feedback—no matter where in the world you are. You can always [send me a tweet](http://www.twitter.com/GavinVerhey/) or ask me a question on [Tumblr](http://gavinverhey.tumblr.com/) and I'll definitely see it.



Additionally—and speaking of global events—I'll be at [Grand Prix Las Vegas](http://magic.wizards.com/en/content/fact-sheet-grand-prix-las-vegas-2015) this weekend, watching history unfold on *Modern Masters* Weekend! It's going to truly be a sight to behold, so definitely tune in. And if you're there, come by and say hi!



I'll talk to you next week, when I dial the clock back and tell you the story of how it all began. Until then, may you have fun playing *Magic* wherever in the world you happen to be.



Have fun!



Gavin



[@GavinVerhey](http://www.twitter.com/GavinVerhey/)



[GavInsight](http://gavinverhey.tumblr.com/)
